2000). 

The arguments for universalist values have been eloquently put forward by Brian Barry in his [3mCulture and Equality [0m(Polity, 2001). 

See David Harvey, [3mThe Condition of Postmodernity [0m(Blackwell, 1980) for a discussion of the influence of the modern media on 
culture. 

[1mูุฑุงุกุงุช ุฅุถุงููุฉ [0m

There are a number of anthologies of postmodernist writings, of which the most committed is Thomas Docherty (ed.), [3mPostmodernism: 
A Reader [0m(Harvester Wheatsheaf, 1993). Ihab Hassanโs seminal articles on postmodernism are collected in his [3mThe Postmodern Turn [0m
(Ohio State University Press, 1987). Derridaโs thoughts on literature are conveniently brought together in Derek Attridge (ed.), [3m
Jacques Derrida: Acts of Literature [0m(Routlege, 1992). Steven Connorโs [3mPostmodernist Culture [0m(Blackwell, 1989) is strongly 
committed to an eclectic range of postmodernist theories. Charles Jencksโs alternative view is neatly summarized in his [3mWhat Is 
Postmodernism? [0m, revised edn. (Academy, 1996). 

For an account of the politics of postmodernism, following Jameson, see Perry Anderson, [3mThe Origins of Postmodernity [0m(Verso 1998). 
On nationalist narratives in the postmodern period, looked at from a broadly postmodernist theoretical standpoint, see Elleke 
Boehmer, [3mColonial and Postcolonial Literature [0m(Oxford University Press, 1995), and Homi Bhabhaโs anthology, [3mNation and Narration [0m
(Routledge, 1990). An excellent early example of the use of Marx, Freud, and deconstruction in literary analysis is Terry 
Eagleton, [3mCriticism and Ideology [0m(NLB, 1976). Useful because they make period contrasts are Patricia Waugh, [3mPractising 
Postmodernism/Reading Modernism [0m(Arnold, 1992) and Peter Brooker, [3mModernism/Postmodernism [0m(Longman, 1992). 

The following are critical but also informative about postmodernist tendencies. For an account of the influence of Marx on 
intellectuals in this period, see J. G. Merquior, [3mWestern Marxism [0m(Paladin, 1986). The new literary theory encountered 
surprisingly little published opposition, but see the interestingly entitled [3mFraud: Literary Theory and the End of English [0mby 
Peter Washington (Fontana, 1989) and Christopher Butler, [3mInterpretation, Deconstruction, and Ideology [0m(Clarendon Press, 1984), 
and, for a general critique, John M. Ellis, [3mAgainst Deconstruction [0m(Princeton University Press, 1989) and Raymond Tallis, [3mNot 
Saussure [0m(Macmillan, 1988). A brilliant account of the relationship of science to political and moral considerations is given by 
Philip Kitcher in his [3mScience, Truth and Democracy [0m(Oxford University Press, 2001). The tendency to the local story attitude of 
postmodern philosophy has inspired a reply from Thomas Nagel, which defends his view of the value and possibility of objectivity 
in philosophy and of the abstracting โview from nowhereโ in ethics, expressed in his [3mThe Last Word [0m(Oxford University Press, 
1997). 

An influential model for non-linguistic phenomena analysed as text was Roland Barthes, [3mSystรจme de la mode [0m(1967; tr. as [3mThe 
Fashion System [0m, Hill and Wang, 1983). This approach became common to all โsemioticโ approaches to culture. For a survey, see 
Robert Hodge and Gunter Kress, [3mSocial Semiotics [0m(Blackwell, 1988). For a study of the different subject positions open to us 
within postmodernist theory and the contemporary novel, see Kim Worthington, [3mSelf as Narrative [0m(Clarendon Press, 1996). For 
Habermasโs critique of postmodernism, see [3minter alia [0mhis [3mThe Philosophical Discourse of Modernity [0m(MIT Press, 1987). Edward 
Lucie-Smith, [3mArt Today [0m(Phaidon, 1995) is an excellent survey of the many current schools of art. An essential resource is to be 
found in Kristine Stiles and Peter Selz (eds), [3mTheories and Documents of Contemporary Art [0m(University of California Press, 1996).
